+def test_missing_evidence_id_fails_loud() -> None:

docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md:147:### Phase 6 — Weighted aggregation (replace count with weight-mass). [L5]
docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md:148:- **Scope:** Replace COUNT aggregation with **origin-cluster weight-mass**, computed by this EXECUTABLE invariant (Codex iter-2 P1-2): group every supporting row by `(claim_cluster_id, origin_cluster_id)`; for each origin cluster L3 designates exactly ONE **canonical origin** (the syndication root / earliest independent publication; the other members are derivative copies — genuinely-INDEPENDENT corroboration has different content and forms its OWN cluster, it does not join an existing one). `cluster_mass = authority_score(canonical origin)`; copy/derivative members are attributed for disclosure ("N copies → 1 origin") but contribute ZERO to the mass. The claim-side weight-mass = Σ of `cluster_mass`, once per origin cluster within the claim cluster. **No row-level term, no averaging, no max-over-copies.** A row joins an existing `origin_cluster_id` only because L3 flagged it a copy of that cluster's canonical origin — so it adds NOTHING to the mass **even if its own `authority_score` is higher than the canonical origin's** (a high-authority verbatim republisher is still derivative; only its own *independent* content would form a new cluster). **Binding invariant (Codex iter-3 + #1161):** for a DATED origin cluster (canonical = earliest publication date) `weight_mass(rows + copied_row) == weight_mass(rows)` for ANY copier authority (strict copy-equality). For an ALL-UNDATED cluster the canonical is the LOWEST-`authority_score` member (conservative-min): the mass is MONOTONICALLY NON-INCREASING under copy additions — a higher-authority copy can NEVER inflate it (the binding no-inflation property), and a lower-authority copy can only LOWER it (honest, never inflating). Either way a copied row can NEVER inflate the false majority. This requires **L3 to emit a stable `origin_cluster_id`, the canonical-origin designation, and membership** (NOT merely an `independent_origin_count` scalar) and L4 to emit `claim_cluster_id`, both BEFORE L5. Without it, copied rows re-inflate the false majority and the vax test fails. Applies in plan-sufficiency AND journal-only adequacy. Per-facet weighting preserved.
docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md:150:- **Clinical source-type veto (Codex iter-1 P1-3 — wired, not a slogan):** a clinical-domain claim requires ≥1 **independent clinical-tier source (T1/T2 clinical)** in its origin-clustered support; if absent, Phase 6 emits a **`not_weight_adequate` / `clinical_source_type_veto`** signal REGARDLESS of news/commercial weight-mass; **Phase 7 (L6) consumes that signal to render ABSTAIN/fringe** (the rendering is Phase 7, not here). Wired to the existing clinical adequacy floor (`corpus_adequacy_gate.py` `_DEFAULT_DOMAIN_THRESHOLDS['clinical']`: `min_t1_count=3`, `min_t1_plus_t2=5`) The source-type veto is OWNED and EMITTED at Phase 6 (the `clinical_source_type_veto` signal); web/news/commercial weight can NEVER substitute for the clinical-tier floor; Phase 7 only RENDERS the resulting ABSTAIN/fringe. **Brief-time note (Codex iter-5 P2):** the per-claim source-type VETO (a claim needs ≥1 independent clinical-tier source) is DISTINCT from the corpus-level clinical adequacy FLOOR (`min_t1_count=3`, `min_t1_plus_t2=5`) — the Phase-6 implementation brief must keep them separate (the veto is a per-claim absence-check; the floor is a corpus threshold). They are not the same gate and must not be conflated.

docs\broad_dr_domain_general_plan.md:59:**GAP F (P0, the money-waster on a broad run that PASSES the gates) — strict_verify drops policy-reasoning sentences.** `provenance_generator.py:957-964` drops any sentence with no provenance token; `:1032-1076` requires every decimal to appear in a cited span; `:813-815,1137-1144` requires ≥2 content-word overlap with a single span; the entailment judge (`:1183-1291`) fails-closed on `NEUTRAL`. Frontier reports are ~50-90% INTEGRATIVE synthesis ("residency is not the same as legal sovereignty"; "demand destruction sabotages supply generation") — sentences that carry no decimal, fuse numbers from two sources, or are NEUTRAL w.r.t. any single span. These get mass-dropped; per-section `<min_kept_fraction` triggers one regen (`multi_section_generator.py:1549`), and if every section keeps zero, `run_honest_sweep_r3.py:2840-2851` writes `abort_no_verified_sections`. Even short of abort, the surviving "Verified Findings" core is a handful of single-fact sentences and the actual analyst reasoning is relegated to the UNVERIFIED Analyst Synthesis block — inverting the frontier bar.

docs\broad_dr_domain_general_plan.md:77:**Step 5 (fixes Gap F — keep the faithfulness wedge, don't weaken it) — domain-adaptive verification.** KEEP `no_provenance_token` drop and the numeric/content-overlap check for any sentence containing a NUMBER — that is the edge that kills Gemini's PR-citation and unhedged-specific failure mode. docs\full_power_polaris_architecture_2026_05_31.md:49:**Stage 8 — 4-role verification (per-claim terminal verdict).** Per atomized claim: **atomize** (Writer splits a sentence with two numbers into two claim-records sharing one span — finer than shipped sentence-level strict_verify) → **Mirror** 2-pass calibration (re-read claim blind to Writer confidence; flag over-claim, emit `calibration_delta`) → **Sentinel** binary RAG-faithfulness gate (grounded y/n; `UNGROUNDED` is **fail-closed** — cannot proceed regardless of Judge) → **Sentinel** qualitative-negation pass (`(did not|no|never|absent|without)+endpoint` must be asserted in the span) → **Judge** terminal 5-enum **VERIFIED / PARTIAL / UNSUPPORTED / FABRICATED / UNREACHABLE** (may downgrade, may NOT upgrade a Sentinel-UNGROUNDED claim) → **python strict_verify** deterministic floor (evidence-id in pool, span bounds valid, every decimal appears verbatim in the span, ≥2 content-word overlap; any failure → DROP, no model override) → **guarded citation-repair** only for span-locality failures (right source, wrong offset): Writer proposes a narrower span from the SAME source, re-judged against the short span; still failing → fail-closed DROP; repair can never invent a source or widen scope. **Model/tool:** `role_pipeline.py` Mirror/Sentinel/Judge (`corpus_relevance_driven_logic.md §4.5`); `generator/strict_verify` (§9.1.3) + M-45 refetch; `openrouter_client.check_family_segregation` (§9.1.1). **Fixes vs shipped:** wires the built-but-not-default gate into the default CLI/UI/queue path (`:3940`); adds atomization, the 5-enum, the negation pass, and the guarded repair (shipped has none — a correct claim with a slightly-off offset is dropped outright, costing coverage). The guarded repair is the corrected design from `project_complete_solution_codex_corrections_2026_05_30` (whole-doc widening would smuggle ungrounded claims; candidate-generator-only + re-judge short span + fail-closed is the safe form).
docs\full_power_polaris_architecture_2026_05_31.md:53:**Stage 10 — Output + audit trail (the category frontier does not contest).** Emits: (O1) a per-sentence VERIFIED/PARTIAL/UNSUPPORTED/FABRICATED/UNREACHABLE/DROPPED **ledger** with the cited span, the Mirror/Sentinel/Judge signals, and the drop-reason — a first-class artifact, not a debug log; (O2) **fail-closed verdict** — if every section fails strict_verify, `report.md` is a pipeline-verdict artifact `abort_no_verified_sections`; rubber-stamp corpus → `abort_corpus_approval_denied` (§9.3); (O3) a **signed audit bundle** (report + ledger + conflict records + `corpus_funnel` + resolved span text, hashed/signed); (O4) the **Proof-Replay split-view** demo centerpiece (click any claim → highlight the exact cited span side-by-side + 4-role verdict chips + decimal-match); (O5) a **saturation/concision report** so concision is auditable, not arbitrary truncation. **Model/tool:** python aggregator over Stage-8 outputs; §9.3 statuses; signed-manifest infra (§9.1); Proof-Replay UI (tasks #448-454, #461). **Fixes vs shipped:** the pipeline emits artifacts but no user-facing ledger, no single signed replayable bundle, and no replay surface; sentences are dropped silently inside strict_verify.

docs\frontier_credibility_intelligence_2026_06_07.md:22:The through-line: **quality is WEIGHT, not COUNT, and the weight must (a) actually drive synthesis, (b) discount non-independent corroboration, and (c) be disclosed per claim.** No deployed system does all three. POLARIS's existing per-sentence `[#ev:id:start-end]` provenance + `strict_verify` is the right substrate; the missing layers are a disclosed credibility prior, an independence/echo-chamber collapse, and a per-claim weight-and-disclose UX.
docs\frontier_credibility_intelligence_2026_06_07.md:55:**Relevance to POLARIS:** OpenAI DR is the closest competitor on citation hygiene and the system to beat on faithfulness. Its "explains why each source was chosen" is prose, not an auditable weight — exactly what POLARIS's disclosed credibility prior + span-bound provenance token out-rigors. The 21% unsupported-citation rate and the 79%→17% degradation curve are the concrete failure modes `strict_verify` (numeric match + content-word span overlap) is built to catch. **Perplexity is the strongest single argument FOR the POLARIS thesis:** most citation-visible product, grounds almost nothing — proof that visible citations without span verification are theater.
docs\frontier_credibility_intelligence_2026_06_07.md:205:**Where POLARIS could LEAD, given per-claim provenance.** POLARIS already has the hardest substrate — per-sentence `[#ev:id:start-end]` tokens + `strict_verify` (numeric match + ≥2 content-word span overlap) + zero-verified-abort. That is the verify-against-span layer the entire faithfulness literature says is missing and the layer a citation chip cannot provide. The lead is to extend that substrate from *provenance disclosure* to **provenance + credibility-weight + independent-origin-count + certainty disclosure per claim** — the union that no competitor offers — and to make the credibility weight (a) domain-conditional, (b) independence-aware, and (c) actually drive composition (not sit beside it as a decoration like Consensus's chips).

docs\credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md:1:# POLARIS Source-Credibility & Multi-Perspective Recommendations Report\n### Driving two revisions to `docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md` — LAYER 1 (scoring) and LAYER 6 (composition + UI)\n\n**Author:** Lead analyst (Claude). **Date:** 2026-06-08.\n**Inputs:** three research streams (per-question adaptive credibility weighting; neutral multi-perspective presentation; friendly UI/artifact patterns).\n**Status:** revision driver. Each layer below states what it **REPLACES** in the Codex-APPROVE'd 2026-06-07 plan, then the concrete mechanism, auditability, reliability, and POLARIS wiring.\n\n**Invariants preserved across both revisions** (these are not negotiable and the revisions do not weaken them): the LLM credibility-judge is **advisory only** — `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks (`provenance_generator.py:1156`) remain the binding faithfulness gate; every new layer is **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs; weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; every displayed aggregate is **one click from the cited `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict**; the credibility prior stays **self-computed and verifier-overridable** (no single external rater hardwired); independence-collapse (`synthesis/independence_collapse.py`) still runs before any weighted tally; the contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / voter-arbiter pipeline** (`roles/role_pipeline.py` + `honest_sweep_integration.py`), open-weight voters only — no parallel path is built.\n\n---\n\n## 1. LAYER 1 (scoring): adaptive per-question credibility-skill, replacing the fixed domain-rubric selector\n\n### 1.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 2a/2b (L1)** selects one of **three fixed reliability rubrics** (clinical → RCT+peer-review+RoB; econ/policy → design-validity; qualitative → CERQual) keyed off the detected domain. That is still a small lookup table: domain → rubric. The operator constraint is explicit — **replace fixed domain rubrics** with a **generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill the LLM applies by reasoning per question**. Research stream #1's central finding is that the frontier (OpenAI, Gemini, Claude) has already moved this way, and that Perplexity's baked-in EEAT/domain-authority scoring is the closest-to-forbidden counter-example (gameable, popularity-biased, ~60% Google-overlap). We copy the reasoned-generic camp.\n\nThe revision: **domain stops being a selector and becomes context that primes one generic skill.** There is exactly one credibility skill; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a hint the skill reasons over ("this is a clinical efficacy question, so weight trial design and RoB heavily"), not a branch that swaps rubrics. This scales to 10,000+ fields with zero per-field config.\n\n### 1.2 The exact mechanism — credibility-skill / guardrail prompt × (reliability × relevance)\n\n**Step A — deterministic signals (POLARIS produces these; unchanged substrate).** `authority_model.score_source_authority` and `tier_classifier` already emit, per source, the field-agnostic primitives: `authority_score [0,1]`, `source_class`, `corroboration_count` (independent-host agreement), `authority_confidence`, `signal_scores` (the A–E sub-scores), plus `junk_class` / `predatory_oa` (`source_class.py:71-89`). Independence-collapse (`independence_collapse.py`) emits `origin_cluster_id` + canonical-origin designation + copy flag. **None of this is replaced.** These are the inspectable, host-name-free, self-computed inputs (LAW VI: zero host literals in code).\n\n**Step B — the credibility skill consumes those signals and weights them per question.** A new pure prompt module, `authority/credibility_skill.py`, runs a **JudgeRank-style 3-step decomposition** (arXiv 2411.00142) — chosen because each step is inspectable text and is itself the audit template:\n\n1. **Query analysis** — identify what THIS question actually needs (the claim type, what would count as strong evidence for it).\n2. **Source analysis** — for each candidate source, a query-AWARE assessment applying **generic SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics**, NOT a domain table. The skill's instruction block encodes the domain-agnostic primacy heuristics that are OpenAI's own deep-research pattern: *prefer the primary/official source over an aggregator or SEO blog; prefer the original paper over a survey/secondary summary; corroborate laterally (does independent coverage agree); weigh source incentives/track record; downgrade stale-but-authoritative and retracted/superseded* (the latter wires to the existing `supersession.py` Phase 3 signal).\n3. **Two-axis judgment with rationale** — emit, per source, **RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE** (the EFSA/OHAT weight-of-evidence two-axis, which POLARIS currently conflates into one tier): reliability = internal validity/method given what the skill read in the signals; relevance = directness to this specific question. The product is the per-question credibility weight. **Crucially, the skill is told its priors are the `authority_model` signals and that it may up- or down-weight them with a stated reason** — it does not invent authority from nothing, and it cannot silently override `authority_confidence=LOW` into a fabricated HIGH (thin OpenAlex/ROR signal stays honestly LOW).\n\n**Output schema (machine-parseable, bound to the schema discipline already in §8.3.9):** per source — `{reliability_score, relevance_score, credibility_weight, rationale_string, signals_cited:[...]}`. The weight is **a visible, revisable rationale string, never a hidden scalar and never a fine-tuned-in behavior** (this is why we reject the CAG fine-tune approach from stream #1: opaque learned weights are exactly the auditability failure POLARIS differentiates against — borrow CAG's *evidence* that credibility-conditioning gives noise robustness, and its three generic dimensions of relevance/timeliness/reliability, but implement them at inference time as a prompt-visible signal).\n\n### 1.3 How it stays AUDITABLE (auditable by construction, not bolted on)\n\nThe judgment IS a reasoning trace, so it is emitted verbatim and **bound to the same provenance substrate POLARIS already has**:\n\n- The per-source `credibility_weight` + `rationale_string` + `signals_cited` attach to the source's `AuthorityResult` as **additive fields** (mirroring how `signal_scores`, `junk_class`, `predatory_oa` are already additive side-outputs on the dataclass), emitted on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n- At claim time, the weight flows into the four Phase-1/Phase-8 disclosure fields on `SentenceVerification` (`credibility_weight`, `independent_origin_count`, `certainty_label`, `span_verdict`), so each verified sentence shows **which source was weighted how, and why**, one click from its `[#ev]` span.\n- Because the skill cites the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from, the rationale is **checkable against the inputs** — a reviewer can confirm "preferred A over B because A is the primary trial-registry entry and B a secondary news summary" against the actual `source_class` values. The rationale is a **claim to verify, not ground truth** (post-hoc rationalization risk per stream #1) — so it is advisory and the binding gate stays `strict_verify`.\n\nThis is the §-1.1-compliant story: no metadata/count/string-presence signal, every weight traceable to a cited span and an inspectable reason.\n\n### 1.4 Reliability and where it fails (and the guardrail)\n\nStream #1 is blunt about the failure modes, and they bound the design: LLMs "treat all retrieved documents as equally valid" unless explicitly steered and over-rely on high-frequency claims (arXiv 2505.17762); AuthorityBench (2603.25092) shows authority perception is **inconsistent across domains and highly prompt-sensitive**, struggles with false authority, and exhibits position/verbosity/self-preference bias. Therefore:\n\n- **The skill is ADVISORY to ranking/selection, never the faithfulness gate.** It changes *which rows are billed/weighted*, not *whether a sentence verifies its span*. `strict_verify`, 4-role/two-family segregation, and the independent `corpus_approval_gate` tier-distribution backstop all still run sequentially.\n- **Bias mitigations baked into the prompt:** score rationale-first then number; randomize candidate order to blunt position bias; run pointwise (per-source) to avoid listwise permutation instability.\n- **Offline validation before trust:** the chosen judge model+prompt is validated on an **AuthorityBench-style harness** (authority-PERCEPTION only, per the §6a no-overstatement correction — not as a volume-vulnerability benchmark) plus the existing vax adversarial fixture, before it is allowed on the shipping path. Calibration (Brier/ECE) on the emitted weights runs in the existing Phase 11 harness.\n- **Capture resistance:** multi-signal, self-computed, verifier-overridable — no NewsGuard/MBFC/Ad Fontes verdict is hardwired as ground truth (the FTC-capture risk).\n\n### 1.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L1\n\n**HAVE:** deterministic authority signals (`authority_model`, `tier_classifier`), the additive `AuthorityResult`/`SentenceVerification` schema, independence-collapse, `scope_templates` domain detection, the JSON-verdict schema discipline.\n**MISSING:** the generic per-question credibility skill itself, and the second (relevance) axis.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 2a/2b):**\n1. `authority/credibility_skill.py` — the pure 3-step (query→source→two-axis-judgment) prompt module emitting `{reliability, relevance, credibility_weight, rationale, signals_cited}`. Domain is an input *hint*, not a rubric switch. (Replaces the fixed-rubric selector in `credibility_prior.py`.)\n2. Add `relevance_score` (and the rationale fields) to `AuthorityResult` (`source_class.py:75`); emit on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n3. Wire the skill's weight into the L5 weight-mass tally and the L7 disclosure fields — advisory input, not a gate.\n4. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; OFF = the legacy single-scalar path, byte-for-byte.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LAYER 6 (composition + UI): neutral multi-perspective + transparent evidence-weight artifact, replacing the forewarning/fringe framing\n\n### 2.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 7 (L6)** composes contested claims as "consensus at high weight + minority attributed at low weight **with explicit forewarning**, medical-misinfo **low-weight/fringe**, ABSTAIN over fabricated balance." The operator directive is to **replace the forewarning/fringe framing** with a **neutral multi-perspective presentation where competing world-views are shown as legitimate, each carrying its real (possibly asymmetric) evidence weight, and the user judges** — no bias, no stamps, no forewarning prose.\n\n### 2.2 The hard tension, named and resolved (do not skip this)\n\nThere is a real conflict between two binding constraints, and both sides have a lethal failure mode:\n\n- The operator wants **no fringe/forewarning stamp, all sides legitimate, no bias.**\n- The **clinical-safety invariant #5** (binding, preserved) plus Dixon-Clarke 2013 (PubMed 23193194, measured harm: falsely-balanced vaccine reporting *reduced* perceived safety and vaccination intent), Wikipedia FRINGE, and §-1.1 all say **equal treatment of unequal evidence is itself bias** and is "lethal in clinical." I am not authorized to drop invariant #5.\n\n**The reconciliation — handed to us nearly verbatim by all three streams: replace the LABEL with the BASIS.** Wikipedia NPOV's "neutral *editing*, not neutral *content*"; GRADE's "show the basis, let the user infer"; the no-warning rule from stream #2 is satisfiable **if and only if the criteria behind any weight are displayed**. So:\n\n- The **system** stamps nothing — no "fringe," no "debunked," no forewarning sentence. That is the neutrality.\n- The **evidence weight** carries the (often asymmetric) truth, rendered as a visible **per-perspective evidence-basis panel** the user reads and judges. The asymmetry — *14 RCTs + 3 systematic reviews [High]* vs *2 case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]* — becomes **visible in the artifact** instead of **asserted in a stamp**. The user infers; the system does not editorialize.\n- "Legitimate" means **shown with its real (possibly low) weight and one-click drill-down to span + verdict** — NOT "shown as equally supported." A genuine world-view dispute with no empirical consensus (values, forecasting) shows steelmanned sides at honest parity; an empirical dispute with consensus shows the real weight distribution.\n- The medical-misinfo case is handled **without the banned word**: its panel is simply **near-empty of independent high-tier basis**, and where there is no independent consensus the claim **ABSTAINs** ("contested; no independent consensus" — reusing existing refuse/unresolved behavior). This preserves invariant #5's *substance* (not normalized as an equal side) while dropping the stamp.\n\nThis is neutral AND anti-false-balance AND §-1.1-safe simultaneously — the operator's "let the user judge" satisfied by *showing the basis*, not by *equalizing the boxes*.\n\n### 2.3 The exact composition mechanism\n\nPer question, the composition path first **diagnoses the contestation type** (this IS the adaptive guardrail, copied from Anthropic's even-handedness "lack-of-consensus" discriminator + OpenAI's seek-the-truth-together):\n\n- **empirical-with-consensus** (vaccines, climate) → due-weight: each side shown, weight proportional to verified-evidence quality; the asymmetry is the message, carried by the basis panel.\n- **genuine-uncertainty** (open scientific questions) → separate *supported* from *open*; sides at honest parity.\n- **values dispute** (politics, ethics) → **steelman each legitimate view** (Ideological Turing Test, neutral terminology, no verdict); no evidence-weight asymmetry asserted because there is no due weight to defer to.\n- **forecasting** (AI-and-jobs) → scenario spread, projective not factual.\n\nEach perspective is gathered through its **own retrieval lens** (MODS-style per-perspective retrieval + citation, arXiv 2502.00322 — raw LLMs silently drop minority views; per-perspective retrieval prevents the drop), then composed via the **existing 4-role / voter-arbiter agreement** (cross-lineage, open-weight voters — the bridging/balanced-panel analog) — **not a new adjudication path**. Reranking-for-balance (arXiv 2506.15925) selects the most balanced faithful candidate, because direct just-prompt-balanced generation empirically skews. **The weight attached to each perspective is evidence QUALITY × independent-origin count, never document count** — else we rebuild Ground News's source-count bias inside the summarizer.\n\n### 2.4 The friendly UI artifact — design\n\nBuilt on the **components that already exist** (#744 citation chip + hover source card, #745 per-claim verdict chip, #747 Proof Replay split-view, #757 report page, #758 claim-anchored compare view) — not designed from scratch.\n\n**The artifact: a claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** that opens from any contested sentence (reusing the compare-view host), containing per legitimate perspective:\n\n1. **A neutral position header** — "Position held by [who], with this evidence behind it" — no "fringe"/"warning"/"debunked". A steelmanned one-line statement of the view in neutral terms.\n2. **An evidence-basis sub-panel (GRADE-style, the load-bearing element):** the study types / source tiers / independent-origin count behind that perspective, rendered as **frequencies, not a percentage or a lone dot** — "*8 of n: RCTs + systematic reviews [High certainty]*" vs "*2 of n: case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]*". The certainty label is acceptable **only because its downgrade criteria are shown** (study design / consistency / directness / independence). This makes the asymmetry self-evident without a stamp.\n3. **Scite-style polarity badges** (supporting / contrasting / contextualizing) on each cited source — **neutral hue + icon + text label, never color alone** (colorblind safety; red=contrasting reads as red=wrong and biases toward consensus — explicitly avoided).\n4. **Drill-down:** every badge, every basis count, every panel is **one click from the raw `[#ev]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict** — the Scite "self-correcting" property: a mis-classified badge is exposed by the citing sentence sitting right behind it, and a meter without drill-down would violate the §-1.1 metadata-audit ban.\n\n**Panel sizing defeats false balance structurally, not with a caveat:** panels are **sized/annotated by real verified-evidence weight**, not equal-width — because equal real estate reads as equal credibility (the false-balance trap), and a caveat is empirically insufficient (Effectiviology / false-balance literature). The asymmetry is *in the layout and the basis panel*, not asserted in prose.\n\n**Three named anti-patterns explicitly rejected** (all from the streams, all as negative templates):\n- **Ground News source-count / coverage bar** — measures who-is-saying-this (volume), not evidence weight; §-1.1 bans source counts as quality signals. If a composition strip is shown at all, its axis is **evidence tier / source type**, never ideology or headcount, and it is kept visually separate from the weight panel so "many sources" never reads as "true."\n- **Bare confidence/credibility score (% or traffic-light dot)** — the best-documented HARM pattern: overconfident displays (80% shown / 70% accurate) pushed AI-advice adoption 57%→69.6%, 64% of users mis-judged calibration, and in a 2025 breast-cancer CDSS high confidence *reduced* diagnostic accuracy via overreliance. POLARIS's honest replacement is the per-sentence VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict against a real span — never a glanceable dot.\n- **Symmetric 50/50 equal-box presentation** — manufactures false balance; the Dixon-Clarke measured harm.\n\n### 2.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L6\n\n**HAVE:** the disclosure substrate (per-sentence `[#ev]` tokens, `strict_verify` verdict ladder, `SentenceVerification` additive fields), the existing 4-role/voter-arbiter agreement, independence-collapse for origin-count, and the full UI component kit (citation chip, verdict chip, Proof Replay, compare view).\n**MISSING:** the contestation-type classifier, per-perspective retrieval + composition that defeats false balance by weight, and the Perspectives artifact rendering basis panels.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 7):**\n1. A **contestation-type classifier** (empirical-consensus / genuine-uncertainty / values / forecasting) priming the composition rule — replaces the fixed forewarning+fringe rule.\n2. **Per-perspective retrieval + balance-rerank composition** over the post-collapse origins, weighting each perspective by verified-evidence quality × independent-origin count (not count).\n3. A **steelman + GRADE-style evidence-basis renderer** feeding a new **claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** in the compare-view host: neutral headers, frequency-framed basis sub-panels, Scite-style neutral polarity badges, full span-verdict drill-down, weight-proportional sizing.\n4. Validated with a **paired-prompt neutrality eval** (Anthropic's open-sourced political-neutrality harness, adapted so it does NOT reward equal treatment of unequal evidence) + the vax adversarial fixture (asserts the asymmetry renders, no stamp, no 50/50).\n5. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; ABSTAIN reuses existing refuse/unresolved behavior; forewarning prose removed, replaced by the basis panel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consolidated "build" summary\n\n| Layer | Replaces (2026-06-07 plan) | POLARIS builds | Binding gate untouched |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **L1 scoring** | Fixed 3-rubric domain selector (Phase 2a/2b) | `credibility_skill.py` — generic 3-step SIFT/lateral-reading skill, reliability×relevance, rationale bound to `AuthorityResult`/`[#ev]`; domain as hint not switch; `relevance_score` axis | `strict_verify` binding; skill advisory; corpus_approval backstop |\n| **L6 composition+UI** | Forewarning + fringe framing (Phase 7) | Contestation-type classifier + per-perspective retrieval/balance-rerank weighted by quality×origin-count + steelman/GRADE-basis "Perspectives" panel (replace label with basis) | 4-role/voter-arbiter reused (no parallel path); ABSTAIN reuses refuse/unresolved; invariant #5 substance preserved |\n\nHonest residual: L1's skill is prompt-sensitive and must clear offline AuthorityBench-style + calibration validation before it is trusted on the shipping path; L6's steelman is the hardest element to audit mechanically (no test certifies an argument is the strongest version vs a disguised strawman — the paired-prompt eval is the best available check, itself a judgment). Both remain advisory; `strict_verify` carries faithfulness.\n\n---\n\n## 4. docs\clinical_rag_sota_deepest_research_2026_05_27.md:28:**The single most expensive belief POLARIS is currently holding that this research overturns:** the operator-locked DeepSeek V4 Pro generator is the WRONG generator for the hallucination-sensitivity dimension. Vectara HHEM-2.3 evaluator (May 2026 leaderboard) ranks V4 Pro at 8.6%, V3.2-Exp at 5.3%, Qwen3-8B at 4.8%, Antgroup Finix S1 32B at 1.8%. All four lower-hallucination options are open-weight non-US. V4 Pro is also notorious for 94% non-abstention on AA-Omniscience (it answers when it doesn't know). The 44.4% refusal rate POLARIS is seeing is V4 Pro's low-abstention pathology being correctly caught by POLARIS's validator. This is a generator-choice problem, not a validator problem. **Per CLAUDE.md §-1.1 + `feedback_route_policy_questions_to_codex.md` I am surfacing this for Codex review, not silently switching.** Operator's "frontier-only, top-notch only" directive was a general capability directive; the dimension-specific data argues for an additional consideration. Most defensible path: keep V4 Pro as primary reasoning generator AND add Qwen3-8B as a parallel "low-hallucination prose finalizer" model in the same ensemble used by CHECK, exploiting the family diversity that POLARIS's two-family invariant (§9.1) already requires.

POLARIS's two-family invariant already requires two distinct LLM lineages — extending to 3-5 and computing entropy / KL across them is mechanical. **Fix:** re-implement CHECK's classifier on POLARIS's existing generator + a Qwen3 mirror + a Llama-3.3 mirror.

docs\process\polaris_task_cycle_proposal_2026_05_28.md:296:**Re-grounding (the literature's core anti-drift fix).** The §3.1 intra-task drift ritual (every 10 tool calls / 15 min) must **re-read the runtime *lock*** (`polaris_runtime_lock.yaml`), not just the issue row. As context fills, the spec is the first thing to fall out of the window; re-injecting the machine-readable lock is exactly the "configurancy / specification-locking + periodic re-verification" pattern. The mechanical question the agent asks is *"which lock checkpoints are unsatisfied?"* (a `verify_lock` query), not *"do I remember the architecture?"*. This is what turns the 4-role drift (the failure that produced I-meta-001) into a structurally-prevented class.
docs\process\polaris_task_cycle_proposal_2026_05_28.md:298:**Why this maps to 2026 best practice:** spec-as-executable-contract + conformance suite (`verify_lock` + CI gate) = the documented fix for "tests pass but coherence collapses." A green test suite is *not* evidence of spec conformance; the lock + attestation gate is. The two-family (now N-way `all_distinct`) generator/evaluator invariant is the literature-confirmed mitigation for same-family judge bias ("popularity trap") — do not relax it for convenience.

docs\process\polaris_gap_analysis_2026_05_28.md:20:**Gap one — the four-role pipeline.** The Generator role is fully wired and real: `src/polaris_graph/generator/multi_section_generator.py` reads the Generator model setting and builds a live client. The other three roles — Mirror, Sentinel, and Judge — are declared as settings in one file, `src/polaris_graph/llm/openrouter_client.py`, and referenced nowhere else. No code ever builds a client for them. There is no calibration pass, no hallucination-detector pass, no final-arbiter pass. The architecture lock at `config/architecture/polaris_runtime_lock.yaml` names all four roles correctly, and a freeze guard in `scripts/dr_benchmark/pathB_run_gate.py` deliberately blocks the gated smoke test until the lock is signed — so today neither the old path nor the new path actually runs four roles. The gap is large. The one main thing to do: build a role-dispatch layer that constructs a client for each of Mirror, Sentinel, and Judge and adds their three call sites after generation. Important wrinkle the operator already decided: two of these models — Cohere Command A+ (Mirror) and Granite Guardian (Sentinel) — are not available on OpenRouter, so they must be self-hosted on rented Vast.ai GPUs, while Generator and Judge stay on OpenRouter. That means the dispatch layer needs two serving modes, and the whole four-role base is blocked on one operator action: the Vast.ai account balance is currently zero and needs credit loaded before Mirror and Sentinel can run anywhere. Also note: the Judge model name in the lock still carries a small typo, but that fix is already approved and in flight under issue I-meta-002 — it is not a fresh discovery.
docs\process\polaris_gap_analysis_2026_05_28.md:24:**Gap three — the snowball knowledge graph.** This one is the furthest from real. What exists is a per-run picture in the web UI at `web/app/runs/[runId]/graph/page.tsx`, with an "expand snowball" button that walks the connections within a single run only — it is a viewer, not a memory. There is one cross-run store in `src/polaris_graph/memory/cross_vector.py`, but it is a flat list of text embeddings with no nodes, edges, entities, or relations, so it is not a knowledge graph at all — and it is empty, with zero claims accumulated, and it is wired only into a dormant pipeline the production sweep never touches. There is no store that saves verified claims across runs, and no code anywhere that checks a new run's claims against what was verified in past runs — so the cross-time contradiction catch you want simply does not exist. The gap is large. The one main thing to do: this is design-only for now under issue I-meta-003, and it is deliberately blocked until the four-role base passes a real dry run. So the honest move is to leave it as design and build it after the four roles work.

def _order_key(row: dict[str, Any], row_index: int) -> tuple:
    """Deterministic canonical-selection order key (canonical = ``min`` over members).

    A DATED row sorts before any undated row; among dated rows the earliest CALENDAR date
    wins and ``authority_score`` is NEVER consulted (so a higher-authority but later-dated
    copy can never steal the canonical origin). Same-date ties break on the STABLE
    evidence_id, then the input index. Codex iter-1/2/3 fixes: dated-beats-undated;
    malformed/non-ISO and non-calendar dates are treated as undated.

    When EVERY member of a cluster is undated there is no date to identify the seed
    positionally, so the canonical is the LOWEST-``authority_score`` member: a higher-
    authority copy can then never become the canonical origin and inflate ``cluster_mass``
    (the load-bearing copy-invariance invariant — Codex iter-4 P1). The evidence_id breaks
    authority ties (NOT the input index), so a prepended copy cannot win on position. A
    later-added LOWER-authority copy may relabel the cluster to itself, but that only ever
    LOWERS the mass — monotonically non-increasing under additions, never inflatable.

    Returns a 5-tuple ``(has_no_date, (y, m, d), auth_rank, evidence_id, row_index)``; the
    ``auth_rank`` slot is a constant ``0.0`` for DATED rows (date decides) and the real
    authority for undated rows (lowest wins).
    """
    eid = str(row.get("evidence_id", "") or "")
    for key in _ORDER_KEYS:
        parsed = _parse_order_date(row.get(key))
        if parsed is not None:
            return (0, parsed, 0.0, eid, row_index)
    authority = row.get("authority_score")
    auth_rank = float(authority) if isinstance(authority, (int, float)) else 0.0
    return (1, (9999, 12, 31), auth_rank, eid, row_index)


def _tokenize(text: str) -> list[str]:
    """Lowercased word-character tokens. Pure stdlib; deterministic."""
    return [t.lower() for t in _TOKEN_RE.findall(text)]


def _term_frequencies(tokens: list[str]) -> dict[str, int]:
    counts: dict[str, int] = {}
    for tok in tokens:
        counts[tok] = counts.get(tok, 0) + 1
    return counts


def _tfidf_cosine_matrix(texts: list[str]) -> list[list[float]]:
    """Pairwise TF-IDF cosine similarity over ``texts`` (pure Python).

    TF = raw term count per document. IDF = ``ln((1 + N) / (1 + df)) + 1``
    (the smoothed, always-positive scikit-learn convention) so a single-doc
    corpus still yields well-defined, non-degenerate vectors. Vectors are
    L2-normalised; cosine of two normalised vectors is their dot product.
    An empty document has a zero vector and cosine 0 with everything.
    """
    n = len(texts)
    token_lists = [_tokenize(t) for t in texts]
    # Document frequency per term.
    doc_freq: dict[str, int] = {}
    for tokens in token_lists:
        for term in set(tokens):
            doc_freq[term] = doc_freq.get(term, 0) + 1
    idf: dict[str, float] = {
        term: math.log((1 + n) / (1 + df)) + 1.0 for term, df in doc_freq.items()
    }
    # Build L2-normalised TF-IDF vectors as sparse dicts.
    vectors: list[dict[str, float]] = []
    for tokens in token_lists:
        tf = _term_frequencies(tokens)
        vec = {term: count * idf[term] for term, count in tf.items()}
        norm = math.sqrt(sum(w * w for w in vec.values()))
        if norm > 0.0:
            vec = {term: w / norm for term, w in vec.items()}
        vectors.append(vec)
    # Pairwise cosine = dot product of normalised vectors.
    matrix = [[0.0] * n for _ in range(n)]
    for i in range(n):
        matrix[i][i] = 1.0 if vectors[i] else 0.0
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            a, b = vectors[i], vectors[j]
            # Iterate the smaller dict for the dot product.
            if len(a) > len(b):
                a, b = b, a
            dot = sum(weight * b.get(term, 0.0) for term, weight in a.items())
            sim = 0.0 if dot < 0.0 else (1.0 if dot > 1.0 else dot)
            matrix[i][j] = sim
            matrix[j][i] = sim
    return matrix


class _UnionFind:
    """Minimal disjoint-set for transitive content-copy clustering."""

    def __init__(self, n: int) -> None:
        self._parent = list(range(n))

    def find(self, x: int) -> int:
        root = x
        while self._parent[root] != root:
            root = self._parent[root]
        # Path compression.
        while self._parent[x] != root:
            self._parent[x], x = root, self._parent[x]
        return root

    def union(self, a: int, b: int) -> None:
        ra, rb = self.find(a), self.find(b)
        if ra != rb:
            # Attach the higher-index root under the lower so the canonical
            # (lowest order-key) tends to stay near the root; canonical choice
            # below is explicit regardless, this only keeps roots stable.
            lo, hi = (ra, rb) if ra < rb else (rb, ra)
            self._parent[hi] = lo


# ── Public API ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────


def collapse_independent_origins(
    rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
    *,
    gov_suffixes: tuple[str, ...],
    similarity_threshold: float = DEFAULT_SIMILARITY_THRESHOLD,
    acceptable_mirror_domains: tuple[str, ...] = DEFAULT_ACCEPTABLE_MIRROR_DOMAINS,
) -> IndependenceCollapseResult:
    """Cluster rows into independent origins; flag derivative copies.

    Args:
        rows: generator-visible evidence rows. Each may carry ``evidence_id``,
            ``source_url``, text (``direct_quote``/``statement``/``text``/
            ``snippet``), an optional publication-order key
            (``published_date``/``publication_date``/``published``/``date``),
            and an optional ``authority_score`` (NOT used for clustering or
            canonical choice — only carried through by the caller).
        gov_suffixes: PSL multi-level gov-suffix tuple from
            ``authority.data_loader.load_authority_data()["psl_gov_suffixes"]``
            — passed in so this module hardcodes NO host/TLD literals.
        similarity_threshold: TF-IDF cosine at/above which two texts are a
            content copy (LAW VI — caller-configurable; default 0.85).
        acceptable_mirror_domains: registrable domains whose cross-host
            content near-duplicates are legitimate mirrors and are NOT
            collapsed on content alone (false-positive bound).

    Returns:
        :class:`IndependenceCollapseResult` with one
        :class:`RowOriginAssignment` per input row (ordered by row index),
        the :class:`OriginCluster` list, and the ``independent_origin_count``.
    """
    rows = list(rows or [])
    n = len(rows)
    threshold = float(similarity_threshold)
    mirror_set = {d.lower() for d in acceptable_mirror_domains}

    if n == 0:
        return IndependenceCollapseResult(
            clusters=[],
            assignments=[],
            raw_row_count=0,
            independent_origin_count=0,
            similarity_threshold=threshold,
        )

    domains = [_row_domain(rows[i], gov_suffixes) for i in range(n)]
    texts = [_row_text(rows[i]) for i in range(n)]
    sim = _tfidf_cosine_matrix(texts)

    uf = _UnionFind(n)
    for i in range(n):
        for j in range(i + 1, n):
            same_domain = bool(domains[i]) and domains[i] == domains[j]
            if same_domain:
                # Same registrable origin (host-collapse primitive): one origin.
                uf.union(i, j)
                continue
            # Cross-domain: collapse only on content near-duplication. A curated
            # acceptable-mirror host (arXiv/SSRN/PMC) only ever collapses with its
            # OWN registrable domain (the same_domain branch above), NEVER via
            # cross-domain content. Otherwise a non-mirror blog that copies the
            # content of TWO different mirror hosts would TRANSITIVELY bridge them
            # into one union-find cluster (Codex iter-1 P2). Skipping any
            # cross-domain union that touches a mirror keeps legitimate mirrors
            # independent on content alone; the rare non-mirror copy of mirror
            # content simply stays its own origin — a safe under-collapse, never a
            # mirror false-merge.
            either_mirror = domains[i] in mirror_set or domains[j] in mirror_set
            if either_mirror:
                continue
            if texts[i] and texts[j] and sim[i][j] >= threshold:
                uf.union(i, j)

    # Group members by union-find root.
    members_by_root: dict[int, list[int]] = {}
    for i in range(n):
        members_by_root.setdefault(uf.find(i), []).append(i)

    clusters: list[OriginCluster] = []
    canonical_of: dict[int, int] = {}      # member index -> canonical index
    cluster_id_of: dict[int, str] = {}     # member index -> origin_cluster_id

    for member_indices in members_by_root.values():
        member_indices = sorted(member_indices)
        # Canonical = earliest-dated origin (authority not consulted), or for an all-undated
        # cluster the LOWEST-authority member (conservative-min, no inflation — Codex #1161).
        canonical_index = min(
            member_indices, key=lambda idx: _order_key(rows[idx], idx)
        )
        # Stable, copy-immune id: derived from the canonical row's EVIDENCE IDENTITY, NOT its
        # input position — so a copy added BEFORE the canonical (prepended) does not shift the
        # index and change the id (Codex iter-2 P2). A missing evidence_id is a FAIL-LOUD data
        # error (Codex #1161), never a position-relative fallback.
        canonical_eid = str(rows[canonical_index].get("evidence_id", "") or "").strip()
        if not canonical_eid:
            raise ValueError(
                "independence_collapse: canonical row is missing 'evidence_id'; a stable "
                "origin_cluster_id requires every evidence row to carry evidence_id "
                "(Codex #1161 — a positional fallback id is not copy-stable)."
            )
        origin_cluster_id = f"origin::{canonical_eid}"
        copy_indices = [i for i in member_indices if i != canonical_index]
        member_hosts = sorted({domains[i] for i in member_indices} - {""})
        clusters.append(
            OriginCluster(
                origin_cluster_id=origin_cluster_id,
                canonical_index=canonical_index,
                member_indices=member_indices,
                copy_indices=copy_indices,
                member_hosts=member_hosts,
            )
        )
        for i in member_indices:
            canonical_of[i] = canonical_index
            cluster_id_of[i] = origin_cluster_id

    clusters.sort(key=lambda c: c.canonical_index)

    assignments = [
        RowOriginAssignment(
            row_index=i,
            origin_cluster_id=cluster_id_of[i],
            canonical_index=canonical_of[i],
            is_canonical_origin=(canonical_of[i] == i),
            is_derivative_copy=(canonical_of[i] != i),
        )
        for i in range(n)
    ]

    return IndependenceCollapseResult(
        clusters=clusters,
        assignments=assignments,
        raw_row_count=n,
        independent_origin_count=len(clusters),
        similarity_threshold=threshold,
    )

 succeeded in 5602ms:

"""Offline unit tests for Phase 4a independence-collapse.

Module under test: ``src/polaris_graph/synthesis/independence_collapse.py``.

THE LOAD-BEARING INVARIANT (plan Phase 4a / Phase 6 copy-invariance):
adding a copied row to an existing cluster — even one whose own
``authority_score`` is HIGHER than the cluster's canonical origin — does NOT
change the cluster SET nor its CANONICAL ORIGIN. So a later weighted tally
over canonical origins (``cluster_mass = authority_score(canonical_origin)``)
cannot be inflated by copies. Proven by
``test_added_high_authority_copy_does_not_change_cluster_set_or_canonical``
and ``test_canonical_never_chosen_by_authority``.

All fixtures are inline literals (LAW VI — no live data, no network, no model).
"""
from __future__ import annotations

from typing import Any

from src.polaris_graph.synthesis.independence_collapse import (
    DEFAULT_ACCEPTABLE_MIRROR_DOMAINS,
    DEFAULT_SIMILARITY_THRESHOLD,
    collapse_independent_origins,
)

# The PSL gov-suffix tuple is passed in by the caller in production; for these
# offline tests a small fixture tuple suffices (no host literals live in the
# module under test). Covers the multi-level suffix path used by
# registrable_domain.
_GOV_SUFFIXES: tuple[str, ...] = ("go.jp", "gc.ca", "gov.uk")

# A press-release body and a near-verbatim syndication of it (>0.85 cosine).
_PRESS_RELEASE = (
    "The agency announced that quarterly emissions fell by twelve percent "
    "following the new industrial regulation introduced last spring across "
    "all twenty member regions of the federation."
)
_SYNDICATED_COPY = (
    "The agency announced that quarterly emissions fell by twelve percent "
    "following the new industrial regulation introduced last spring across "
    "all twenty member regions of the federation, officials said."
)
# A genuinely different finding (independent reporting) — low cosine to above.
_INDEPENDENT_FINDING = (
    "A separate university study measured rainfall totals over the alpine "
    "watershed and reported a record snowpack deficit for the third "
    "consecutive winter season."
)


def _row(
    evidence_id: str,
    url: str,
    text: str,
    *,
    authority_score: float | None = None,
    **extra: Any,
) -> dict[str, Any]:
    row: dict[str, Any] = {
        "evidence_id": evidence_id,
        "source_url": url,
        "direct_quote": text,
    }
    if authority_score is not None:
        row["authority_score"] = authority_score
    row.update(extra)
    return row


def _collapse(rows: list[dict[str, Any]], **kw: Any):
    return collapse_independent_origins(rows, gov_suffixes=_GOV_SUFFIXES, **kw)


# ── Basic shape / edge cases ────────────────────────────────────────────────


def test_empty_input_returns_empty_result() -> None:
    result = _collapse([])
    assert result.raw_row_count == 0
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 0
    assert result.clusters == []
    assert result.assignments == []


def test_single_row_is_its_own_canonical_origin() -> None:
    result = _collapse([_row("e0", "https://newsone.com/a", _PRESS_RELEASE)])
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    assert len(result.assignments) == 1
    a = result.assignments[0]
    assert a.is_canonical_origin is True
    assert a.is_derivative_copy is False
    assert a.canonical_index == 0


def test_every_input_row_has_exactly_one_assignment() -> None:
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://a.com/x", _PRESS_RELEASE),
        _row("e1", "https://b.com/y", _INDEPENDENT_FINDING),
        _row("e2", "https://c.com/z", _SYNDICATED_COPY),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert [a.row_index for a in result.assignments] == [0, 1, 2]
    # Partition check: canonical + copy flags are mutually exclusive & total.
    for a in result.assignments:
        assert a.is_canonical_origin != a.is_derivative_copy


# ── Host-collapse primitive (layered on corroboration.registrable_domain) ───


def test_same_registrable_domain_collapses_to_one_origin() -> None:
    """Two different texts on subdomains of one institution = one origin."""
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://news.example.com/a", _PRESS_RELEASE),
        _row("e1", "https://www.example.com/b", _INDEPENDENT_FINDING),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    assert sorted(cluster.member_indices) == [0, 1]
    assert cluster.member_hosts == ["example.com"]


def test_distinct_domains_distinct_content_stay_independent() -> None:
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://a.com/x", _PRESS_RELEASE),
        _row("e1", "https://b.com/y", _INDEPENDENT_FINDING),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 2


# ── Content-copy collapse (TF-IDF cosine >= threshold) ──────────────────────


def test_near_verbatim_copy_across_domains_collapses() -> None:
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://origin-wire.com/release", _PRESS_RELEASE),
        _row("e1", "https://reprint-daily.com/story", _SYNDICATED_COPY),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    assert sorted(cluster.member_indices) == [0, 1]
    assert cluster.canonical_index == 0  # earliest by corpus order
    assert cluster.copy_indices == [1]


def test_many_copies_of_one_release_collapse_to_one_origin() -> None:
    """N near-verbatim copies of one press release -> independent_origin==1."""
    rows = [_row("e0", "https://origin-wire.com/release", _PRESS_RELEASE)]
    for i in range(1, 50):
        rows.append(
            _row(f"e{i}", f"https://reprint{i}.com/story", _SYNDICATED_COPY)
        )
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.raw_row_count == 50
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    assert result.clusters[0].canonical_index == 0
    assert len(result.clusters[0].copy_indices) == 49


def test_two_distinct_findings_with_copies_yield_two_origins() -> None:
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://wire-a.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE),
        _row("e1", "https://reprint-a.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY),   # copy of e0
        _row("e2", "https://univ-b.edu/study", _INDEPENDENT_FINDING),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 2


# ── Acceptable-mirror allowlist (false-positive bound) ──────────────────────


def test_acceptable_mirror_hosts_not_collapsed_on_content_alone() -> None:
    """Same paper text on two scholarly mirror hosts stays TWO origins."""
    paper_text = (
        "We present a transformer variant whose attention cost scales "
        "linearly with sequence length while preserving downstream accuracy "
        "on the standard long-range benchmark suite."
    )
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://arxiv.org/abs/2401.00001", paper_text),
        _row("e1", "https://ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1", paper_text),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    # Both are acceptable-mirror domains -> NOT collapsed on content.
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 2


def test_mirror_allowlist_still_collapses_same_domain_copies() -> None:
    """The allowlist suppresses CROSS-host content-collapse only; two copies
    on the SAME mirror host are still one origin (host-collapse primitive)."""
    paper_text = (
        "We present a transformer variant whose attention cost scales "
        "linearly with sequence length while preserving downstream accuracy."
    )
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://arxiv.org/abs/2401.00001", paper_text),
        _row("e1", "https://arxiv.org/abs/2401.00001v2", paper_text),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1


def test_mirror_host_not_collapsed_with_cross_domain_copy() -> None:
    """A mirror host (arXiv) only collapses within its OWN registrable domain,
    NEVER via cross-domain content — so a non-mirror blog copying an arXiv
    abstract stays a SEPARATE origin. This keeps mirrors immune to being
    transitively bridged through a content copy (Codex iter-1 P2); the rare
    blog-copy-of-a-paper is a safe under-collapse, never a mirror false-merge."""
    paper_text = (
        "We present a transformer variant whose attention cost scales "
        "linearly with sequence length while preserving downstream accuracy "
        "on the standard long-range benchmark suite of nine tasks."
    )
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://arxiv.org/abs/2401.00001", paper_text),
        _row("e1", "https://random-blog.com/repost", paper_text),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 2


def test_blog_copying_two_mirrors_does_not_merge_the_mirrors() -> None:
    """Codex iter-1 P2 regression: a non-mirror blog whose content matches BOTH
    arXiv and PMC must NOT transitively bridge the two mirror hosts into one
    origin. arXiv, PMC, and the blog stay THREE independent origins."""
    paper_text = (
        "We present a transformer variant whose attention cost scales "
        "linearly with sequence length while preserving downstream accuracy "
        "on the standard long-range benchmark suite of nine tasks."
    )
    rows = [
        _row("arxiv", "https://arxiv.org/abs/2401.00001", paper_text),
        _row("pmc", "https://ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1", paper_text),
        _row("blog", "https://random-blog.com/repost", paper_text),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 3


# ── THE INVARIANT: copies cannot change the cluster set or canonical ────────


def test_added_high_authority_copy_does_not_change_cluster_set_or_canonical() -> None:
    """Load-bearing copy-invariance proof.

    Baseline: one canonical origin (low authority) + one copy.
    Then add ANOTHER copy whose own authority_score is far HIGHER than the
    canonical's. The cluster set and the canonical origin MUST be unchanged,
    so a weight tally over canonical origins cannot be inflated by the copy.
    """
    base = [
        _row("origin", "https://wire.com/release", _PRESS_RELEASE,
             authority_score=0.20),
        _row("copy1", "https://reprint1.com/s", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
             authority_score=0.30),
    ]
    base_result = _collapse(base)
    assert base_result.independent_origin_count == 1
    base_cluster = base_result.clusters[0]
    base_canonical_eid = base[base_cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"]
    assert base_canonical_eid == "origin"

    # Add a HIGHER-authority verbatim republisher.
    with_high_authority_copy = base + [
        _row("copy2_high_auth", "https://bigsite.com/s", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
             authority_score=0.99),
    ]
    result = _collapse(with_high_authority_copy)

    # Still exactly ONE independent origin.
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    # Canonical origin is STILL the original low-authority seed.
    assert with_high_authority_copy[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "origin"
    # The high-authority copier is flagged derivative, not canonical.
    high = next(
        a for a in result.assignments
        if with_high_authority_copy[a.row_index]["evidence_id"] == "copy2_high_auth"
    )
    assert high.is_derivative_copy is True
    assert high.is_canonical_origin is False
    # The stable origin_cluster_id is UNCHANGED by the copy addition.
    assert cluster.origin_cluster_id == base_cluster.origin_cluster_id


def test_canonical_never_chosen_by_authority() -> None:
    """Even if a derivative copy has the single highest authority in the
    cluster, the canonical is the earliest/seed member, never the highest
    authority. Authority is not consulted for the canonical choice."""
    rows = [
        _row("seed", "https://origin.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE,
             authority_score=0.10),                    # earliest, low authority
        _row("loud_copy", "https://loud.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
             authority_score=1.00),                    # later, top authority
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    assert rows[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "seed"
    assert cluster.copy_indices == [1]


def test_undated_prepended_higher_authority_copy_cannot_steal_canonical() -> None:
    """Codex iter-4 P1 regression: when EVERY member is undated, the canonical is the
    LOWEST-authority member (not the first by input index), so an undated higher-authority
    copy PREPENDED before the seed cannot become canonical or inflate cluster_mass, and the
    origin_cluster_id stays stable."""
    seed = _row("seed", "https://origin.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE, authority_score=0.10)
    base_id = _collapse([seed]).clusters[0].origin_cluster_id
    high_copy = _row("loud", "https://loud.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY, authority_score=0.99)
    rows = [high_copy, seed]  # PREPEND the undated higher-authority copy before the seed
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    # Canonical is the lowest-authority seed, NOT the prepended high-authority copy.
    assert rows[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "seed"
    assert cluster.origin_cluster_id == base_id
    loud = next(a for a in result.assignments if rows[a.row_index]["evidence_id"] == "loud")
    assert loud.is_derivative_copy is True


def test_undated_high_authority_copy_cannot_outrank_dated_canonical() -> None:
    """Codex iter-1 P1 regression: a DATED canonical origin + an UNDATED copy
    whose own authority is far higher. The undated copy must NOT become the
    canonical (an undated row can never outrank a dated origin), so the cluster
    mass over the canonical is uninflatable."""
    base = [
        _row("dated_origin", "https://wire.com/release", _PRESS_RELEASE,
             authority_score=0.15, published_date="2024-02-01"),
    ]
    assert _collapse(base).clusters[0].canonical_index == 0

    rows = base + [
        _row("undated_high_auth", "https://bigsite.com/s", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
             authority_score=0.99),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    # Canonical is STILL the dated origin, never the undated high-authority copy.
    assert rows[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "dated_origin"
    undated = next(
        a for a in result.assignments
        if rows[a.row_index]["evidence_id"] == "undated_high_auth"
    )
    assert undated.is_derivative_copy is True


def test_origin_cluster_id_stable_under_prepended_copy() -> None:
    """Codex iter-2 P2 regression: origin_cluster_id derives from the canonical row's
    EVIDENCE IDENTITY, not its input position — so a copy added BEFORE the canonical
    (prepended) does not change the cluster id even though the canonical's index shifts."""
    origin = _row("origin", "https://wire.com/release", _PRESS_RELEASE,
                  published_date="2024-02-01")
    base_id = _collapse([origin]).clusters[0].origin_cluster_id
    assert base_id == "origin::origin"

    copy = _row("copycat", "https://aggregator.com/x", _SYNDICATED_COPY)
    rows = [copy, origin]  # PREPEND the derivative copy before the canonical origin
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    # Canonical is still the dated origin (its index is now 1), and the id is unchanged.
    assert rows[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "origin"
    assert cluster.origin_cluster_id == base_id


def test_malformed_non_iso_date_copy_cannot_become_canonical() -> None:
    """Codex iter-2 P1 regression: a derivative copy whose published_date is malformed /
    non-ISO (day-first '01/01/2099') is treated as UNDATED — it can NOT lexically outrank
    the canonical's real ISO date and steal canonical."""
    origin = _row("origin", "https://wire.com/release", _PRESS_RELEASE,
                  published_date="2024-01-01")
    copy = _row("copycat", "https://aggregator.com/x", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
                published_date="01/01/2099")  # day-first, NOT ISO -> treated as undated
    rows = [origin, copy]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    assert rows[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "origin"
    copy_assignment = next(
        a for a in result.assignments if rows[a.row_index]["evidence_id"] == "copycat"
    )
    assert copy_assignment.is_derivative_copy is True


def test_invalid_calendar_date_copy_cannot_become_canonical() -> None:
    """Codex iter-3 P1 regression: an ISO-SHAPED but non-calendar date (2024-02-31 — Feb has
    no 31st) is treated as UNDATED via real datetime validation, so it cannot outrank a real
    2024-03-01 origin and steal canonical (it would have, since (2024,2,31) < (2024,3,1))."""
    origin = _row("origin", "https://wire.com/release", _PRESS_RELEASE,
                  published_date="2024-03-01")
    copy = _row("copycat", "https://aggregator.com/x", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
                published_date="2024-02-31")  # Feb 31 — not a real date -> treated as undated
    rows = [origin, copy]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    assert rows[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "origin"


def test_canonical_uses_explicit_publication_order_when_present() -> None:
    """When a publication-date key is present, the EARLIEST date is canonical
    even if it appears later in corpus order — still order-based, never
    authority-based."""
    rows = [
        # Later date, appears first in corpus order, higher authority.
        _row("later_pub", "https://a.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE,
             authority_score=0.90, published_date="2025-06-01"),
        # Earlier date, appears second, lower authority -> should be canonical.
        _row("earlier_pub", "https://b.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
             authority_score=0.10, published_date="2025-01-15"),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 1
    cluster = result.clusters[0]
    assert rows[cluster.canonical_index]["evidence_id"] == "earlier_pub"


def test_copy_addition_is_order_independent_for_canonical() -> None:
    """Re-ordering the copies in the input does not change which row is
    canonical (the seed) nor the cluster set."""
    seed = _row("seed", "https://origin.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE,
                authority_score=0.10, published_date="2024-01-01")
    copy_a = _row("ca", "https://a.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
                  authority_score=0.95, published_date="2024-05-01")
    copy_b = _row("cb", "https://b.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY,
                  authority_score=0.99, published_date="2024-09-01")
    r1 = _collapse([seed, copy_a, copy_b])
    r2 = _collapse([copy_b, seed, copy_a])
    assert r1.independent_origin_count == r2.independent_origin_count == 1
    assert r1.clusters[0].member_hosts == r2.clusters[0].member_hosts
    # Canonical is the seed in both orderings.
    assert (
        [seed, copy_a, copy_b][r1.clusters[0].canonical_index]["evidence_id"]
        == "seed"
    )
    assert (
        [copy_b, seed, copy_a][r2.clusters[0].canonical_index]["evidence_id"]
        == "seed"
    )


# ── Emitted-contract groupability (Phase 6 can group by origin_cluster_id) ──


def test_origin_cluster_id_is_stable_and_groupable() -> None:
    """Every row carries a stable origin_cluster_id; grouping assignments by
    it reproduces the cluster membership (what Phase 6's weight-mass needs)."""
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://wire.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE),
        _row("e1", "https://reprint.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY),     # copy of e0
        _row("e2", "https://univ.edu/study", _INDEPENDENT_FINDING),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    grouped: dict[str, list[int]] = {}
    for a in result.assignments:
        grouped.setdefault(a.origin_cluster_id, []).append(a.row_index)
    # Exactly one id per cluster; membership matches the cluster objects.
    assert len(grouped) == result.independent_origin_count
    for cluster in result.clusters:
        assert sorted(grouped[cluster.origin_cluster_id]) == sorted(
            cluster.member_indices
        )
    # Each cluster has exactly one canonical row.
    for cluster in result.clusters:
        canonicals = [
            a for a in result.assignments
            if a.origin_cluster_id == cluster.origin_cluster_id
            and a.is_canonical_origin
        ]
        assert len(canonicals) == 1
        assert canonicals[0].row_index == cluster.canonical_index


# ── Configurable threshold (LAW VI) ─────────────────────────────────────────


def test_threshold_is_caller_configurable() -> None:
    """Raising the threshold above the pair's cosine prevents collapse;
    proves the 0.85 default is config, not a hardcoded magic gate."""
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://a.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE),
        _row("e1", "https://b.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY),
    ]
    collapsed = _collapse(rows, similarity_threshold=0.85)
    assert collapsed.independent_origin_count == 1
    # An impossibly high threshold disables content-collapse entirely.
    not_collapsed = _collapse(rows, similarity_threshold=1.0001)
    assert not_collapsed.independent_origin_count == 2
    assert not_collapsed.similarity_threshold == 1.0001


def test_result_reports_default_threshold() -> None:
    result = _collapse([_row("e0", "https://a.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE)])
    assert result.similarity_threshold == DEFAULT_SIMILARITY_THRESHOLD


def test_default_mirror_allowlist_contains_curated_registrable_domains() -> None:
    # Entries are in eTLD+1 form (the space the comparison uses): PMC's
    # ncbi.nlm.nih.gov collapses to nih.gov, so the entry is nih.gov.
    assert "arxiv.org" in DEFAULT_ACCEPTABLE_MIRROR_DOMAINS
    assert "ssrn.com" in DEFAULT_ACCEPTABLE_MIRROR_DOMAINS
    assert "nih.gov" in DEFAULT_ACCEPTABLE_MIRROR_DOMAINS


# ── Purity: caller rows are never mutated ───────────────────────────────────


def test_input_rows_are_not_mutated() -> None:
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://a.com/r", _PRESS_RELEASE, authority_score=0.2),
        _row("e1", "https://b.com/r", _SYNDICATED_COPY, authority_score=0.9),
    ]
    snapshot = [dict(r) for r in rows]
    _collapse(rows)
    assert rows == snapshot  # no origin_cluster_id/flags written onto inputs


def test_empty_text_rows_do_not_falsely_collapse() -> None:
    """Two rows with no text and different domains must NOT collapse (a zero
    vector has cosine 0 with everything — never a false copy)."""
    rows = [
        _row("e0", "https://a.com/r", ""),
        _row("e1", "https://b.com/r", ""),
    ]
    result = _collapse(rows)
    assert result.independent_origin_count == 2


def test_missing_evidence_id_fails_loud() -> None:
    """Codex #1161: a canonical row without evidence_id raises (no position-relative fallback
    id). Real evidence rows always carry evidence_id; a missing one is a data bug, fail-loud."""

    try:
        _collapse(rows)

        raised = True
        assert "evidence_id" in str(exc)
    assert raised, "a canonical row missing evidence_id must fail loud, not fall back to an index id"
